ðŸ’¬ [107] tuulikauri (8:25:39 PM)
If you want it to wait you can do this instead. In general. Instead of delay() this doesnt make the whole program stop and wait.
```ino
unsigned long previousMillis = 0;
const long actionInterval= 1000; //1000 millis = 1 second

void loop(){
  unsigned long currentMillis = millis();
  if (currentMillis - previousMillis >= actionInterval) {
    previousMillis = currentMillis;
    //do the actions you want here
  }
}//end loop
```

// ConstantSpeed.pde
// -*- mode: C++ -*-
//
// Shows how to run AccelStepper in the simplest,
// fixed speed mode with no accelerations
/// \author  Mike McCauley (mikem@airspayce.com)
// Copyright (C) 2009 Mike McCauley
// $Id: ConstantSpeed.pde,v 1.1 2011/01/05 01:51:01 mikem Exp mikem $

```

#include <AccelStepper.h>

AccelStepper stepper; // Defaults to AccelStepper::FULL4WIRE (4 pins) on 2, 3, 4, 5

void setup()
{  
   stepper.setMaxSpeed(1000);
   stepper.setSpeed(50);    
}

void loop()
{  
   stepper.runSpeed();
}
```

ðŸ’¬ [170] thekoy0 (8:49:15 PM)
```


// Define pin connections
const int dirPin = 6;
const int stepPin = 5;
const int sleepPin = 7;
const int resetPin = 8;
const int stepsPerRevolution = 200;

const int steps = 200;
int stepDelay;
#include <AccelStepper.h>

AccelStepper stepper(1, stepPin, dirPin); // Stepper motor interface

void setup() {
  digitalWrite(sleepPin, HIGH);
  digitalWrite(resetPin, HIGH);
  stepper.setMaxSpeed(1000); // Set maximum speed
  stepper.setAcceleration(500); // Set acceleration
}

void loop() {
  stepper.moveTo(200); // Move forward 200 steps
  stepper.runToPosition(); // Block until position is reached

  delay(1000); // Wait for 1 second

  stepper.moveTo(-200); // Move back 200 steps
  stepper.runToPosition(); // Block until position is reached

  delay(1000); // Wait for 1 second
}
```

ðŸ’¬ [1] nick0470 (4:59:01 AM)
I am trying to use a arduino uno to add some buttons to my logitech g923 steeringwheel. I entered code into it using simhub but I need a way to flip the series imput into a keypress. I know I can get a Leonardo but preferably I use this Arduino.

ðŸŽ¯ [2] toph2814 (5:18:55 AM) [REPLY]
understand that to be plug & play with most modern operating systems *(Windows, Linux, Android, MacOS, iOs)*  the USB device has to be `HID`-compliant *(`H`uman `I`nterface `D`evice ~a standard)* ...
ðŸ¤“ unlike a *Leonardo (or other HID compliant microcontroller development boards like the Pro Micro, RP2040-based ones, & ESP32s)*, an *Arduino UNO*  is not... so you'll need software running on the operating system side to take the serial information from it to simulate keystrokes.

ðŸ’¬ [3] toph2814 (5:20:44 AM)
ðŸ˜“ although there are ways to force an *UNO*  into HID compliance, making a mistake during the process *(which from what I've read doesn't always work on all clones or knockoffs out there)*  will render your *UNO*  board useless... which is why I *(& many helpers in this server)*  do not recommend it.

ðŸ’¬ [4] toph2814 (5:21:05 AM)
*(... specially since alternative boards are a lot cheaper & much more compact)*

ðŸ’¬ [5] nick0470 (5:22:27 AM) [REPLY]
So I should just give up and go for a leonardo?

ðŸ’¬ [6] toph2814 (6:23:45 AM) [REPLY]
or one of the many more capable HID compliant options...

Hi !
I am trying to make my Arduino Nano 33 BLE communicate with my phone via BLE.

I made this code, based on the example code from the HCSR04 library.

```
#include <HCSR04.h>
#include <HardwareBLESerial.h>

HardwareBLESerial &bleSerial = HardwareBLESerial::getInstance();

UltraSonicDistanceSensor distanceSensor(18, 19);  // Initialize sensor that uses digital pins 13 and 12.

float d = 0.0;

void setup () {
    Serial.begin(9600);  // We initialize serial connection so that we could print values from sensor.

  if (!bleSerial.beginAndSetupBLE("DetecteurArduino")) {
    while (true) {
      Serial.println("failed to initialize HardwareBLESerial!");
      delay(1000);
    }
  }

  Serial.println("Mmmh...");

  // wait for a central device to connect
  while (!bleSerial);

  Serial.println("HardwareBLESerial central device connected!");

  delay(1000);

}

void loop () {
    bleSerial.poll();

    float val = distanceSensor.measureDistanceCm();
    d = -1.0 * val;
    Serial.println(d); // debug USB

    bleSerial.print(d); // BLE
    bleSerial.write(10);        // saut de ligne

    delay(500);
}
```

Since my captor is not connected right now, distanceSensor.measureDistanceCm() always equals -1.00.
Interestingly, my code works fine if I don't use distanceSensor.measureDistanceCm(), and juste put met = 1.00, which seems absurd to me. Any idea ?

ðŸŽ¯ [2] m_a_v_e_r_i_c_k (10:00:52 AM) [REPLY]
If you have wiring between the two hardware serial ports, uploads will fail.
The same UART connections are used for communication with the computer.
If you want to retain the ability to program the MCU, you could use the SoftwareSerial library.

ðŸ’¬ [3] diamonddback (12:59:34 PM)
```ino
void setup() {
  Serial.begin(9600);

  DDRB &= ~(1 << DDB2);    
  PORTB |= (1 << PORTB2);   
}

void loop() {
  bool pin16State = !(PINB & (1 << PINB2));
  if (pin16State) {
    Serial.println("8");
  } else {
    Serial.println("no button is pressed");
  }

  delay(100); // Optional debounce
}
```
Please try this code, and post a real image of your board for us to look at clear and detailed image.@t0biK_

ðŸ’¬ [63] diamonddback (3:05:50 PM)
There is no physical "pin 16" on the hardware. To simplify coding for new users, we abstract the hardware level to a value we refer to as "16," which is then displayed on the board. This allows users to easily identify and control what they perceive as "pin 16." Occasionally, board manufacturers may omit or mislabel this abstraction, leading to control of an unintended pin. To address this, I bypassed the standard library and directly manipulated the underlying hardware to activate the intended pin, which is labeled as "16."

ðŸ’¬ [1] faxmachinelover (4:43:05 PM)
how to flash an esp32 without using the usb?

ðŸ’¬ [2] m_a_v_e_r_i_c_k (4:43:51 PM) [REPLY]
Over the air (OTA) using WiFi.

ðŸ’¬ [3] faxmachinelover (4:44:45 PM)
cool, ill look into it

ðŸ’¬ [4] faxmachinelover (4:44:55 PM)
do you know about a solution using wires?

ðŸŽ¯ [5] .pseud0 (4:45:36 PM) [REPLY]
If you can get a UART connection to the Boot UART (aka TXD0 RXD0) and a way to reset the chip ito bootloader (usually via EN and IO0), then you can flash via UART.

ðŸ’¬ [6] .pseud0 (4:45:48 PM)
In fact, the USB port is just a USB to UART converter. The actual flashing goes via UART.
